name: Westminster Abbey (The Collegiate Church of St Peter)</i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Designated</th><td>\n24 February 1958</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Reference&#160;no.</th><td>\n1291494<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><th colspan="2">\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Westminster Abbey</b>, formally titled the <b>Collegiate Church of St Peter at Westminster</b>, is a large, mainly <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Abbey_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbey church">abbey church</a> in the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westminster" title="City of Westminster">City of Westminster</a>, London, England, just to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a>. It is one of the United Kingdom\'s most notable religious buildings and the traditional place of <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">coronation</a> and burial site for <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="List of monarchs of England">English</a> and, later, <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_monarchs" title="List of British monarchs">British</a> monarchs. The building itself was a Benedictine monastic church until the monastery was <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">dissolved</a> in 1539. Between 1540 and 1556, the abbey had the status of a <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedral</a>. Since 1560, the building is no longer an <a href="/wiki/Abbey" title="Abbey">abbey</a> or a cathedral, having instead the status of a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> "<a href="/wiki/Royal_Peculiar" title="Royal Peculiar">Royal Peculiar</a>"\xe2\x80\x94a church responsible directly to the sovereign.\n</p><p>According to a tradition first reported by <a href="/wiki/Sulcard" title="Sulcard">Sulcard</a> in about 1080, a church was founded at the site (then known as <a href="/wiki/Thorney_Island_(London)" title="Thorney Island (London)">Thorn Ey (Thorn Island)</a>) in the seventh century, at the time of <a href="/wiki/Mellitus" title="Mellitus">Mellitus</a>, a Bishop of London. Construction of the present church began in 1245, on the orders of <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">King Henry III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the coronation of <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> in 1066, all coronations of English and British monarchs have been in Westminster Abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-History_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coronations_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coronations-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> There have been 16 royal weddings at the abbey since 1100.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#1042:_Edward_the_Confessor_starts_rebuilding_St_Peter&#39;s_Abbey"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">1042: Edward the Confessor starts rebuilding St Peter\'s Abbey</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Construction_of_the_present_church"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Construction of the present church</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#16th_and_17th_centuries:_dissolution_and_restoration"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">16th and 17th centuries: dissolution and restoration</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-5"><a href="#1540\xe2\x80\x931550:_10_years_as_a_cathedral"><span class="tocnumber">1.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">1540\xe2\x80\x931550: 10 years as a cathedral</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-6"><a href="#After_1550:_turbulent_times"><span class="tocnumber">1.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">After 1550: turbulent times</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#1722\xe2\x80\x931745:_Western_towers_constructed"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">1722\xe2\x80\x931745: Western towers constructed</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Second_World_War"><span class="tocnumber">1.5</span> <span class="toctext">Second World War</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Post-war"><span class="tocnumber">1.6</span> <span class="toctext">Post-war</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Gallery"><span class="tocnumber">1.7</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Coronations"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Coronations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Royal_weddings"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Royal weddings</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Chronology"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Chronology</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Dean_and_Chapter"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Dean and Chapter</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Burials_and_memorials"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Burials and memorials</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Schools"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Schools</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Organ"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Organ</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Bells"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Bells</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Chapter_house"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Chapter house</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Museum"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Museum</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Gallery_2"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A late tradition claims that Aldrich, a young fisherman on the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a>, had a <a href="/wiki/Vision_(spirituality)" title="Vision (spirituality)">vision</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a> near the site. This seems to have been quoted as the origin of the salmon that Thames fishermen offered to the abbey in later years \xe2\x80\x93 a custom still observed annually by the <a href="/wiki/Worshipful_Company_of_Fishmongers" title="Worshipful Company of Fishmongers">Fishmongers\' Company</a>. The recorded origins of the Abbey date to the 960s or early 970s, when <a href="/wiki/Saint_Dunstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Dunstan">Saint Dunstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edgar_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar of England">King Edgar</a> installed a community of <a href="/wiki/Benedictine" class="mw-redirect" title="Benedictine">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Monk" title="Monk">monks</a> on the site.<sup id="cite_ref-wpage_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpage-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1042:_Edward_the_Confessor_starts_rebuilding_St_Peter.27s_Abbey"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1042:_Edward_the_Confessor_starts_rebuilding_St_Peter\'s_Abbey">1042: Edward the Confessor starts rebuilding St Peter\'s Abbey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1042: Edward the Confessor starts rebuilding St Peter&#039;s Abbey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg/220px-BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg/330px-BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg/440px-BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg 2x" data-file-width="732" data-file-height="357" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BayeuxTapestryScene26.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Peter\'s Abbey at the time of Edward\'s funeral, depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Bayeux_Tapestry" title="Bayeux Tapestry">Bayeux Tapestry</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1042 and 1052, King <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a> began rebuilding St Peter\'s Abbey to provide himself with a royal burial church. It was the first church in England built in the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> style. The building was completed around 1060 and was consecrated on 28 December 1065, only a week before Edward\'s death on 5 January 1066.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he was buried in the church; and, nine years later, his wife <a href="/wiki/Edith_of_Wessex" title="Edith of Wessex">Edith</a> was buried alongside him.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> His successor, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Godwinson" title="Harold Godwinson">Harold II</a>, was probably crowned in the abbey, although the first documented coronation is that of <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> later the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The only extant depiction of Edward\'s abbey, together with the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a>, is in the <a href="/wiki/Bayeux_Tapestry" title="Bayeux Tapestry">Bayeux Tapestry</a>. Some of the lower parts of the monastic dormitory, an extension of the South Transept, survive in the Norman Undercroft of the Great School, including a door said to come from the previous <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Saxon</a> abbey. Increased endowments supported a community increased from a dozen monks in Dunstan\'s original foundation, up to a maximum about eighty monks.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_of_the_present_church">Construction of the present church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Construction of the present church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Construction of the present church began in 1245 by <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a><sup id="cite_ref-History_\xe2\x80\x93_Westminster_Abbey_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_\xe2\x80\x93_Westminster_Abbey-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> who selected the site for his burial.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:London_westminster_1894.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/London_westminster_1894.jpg/220px-London_westminster_1894.jpg" width="220" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/London_westminster_1894.jpg/330px-London_westminster_1894.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/London_westminster_1894.jpg/440px-London_westminster_1894.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1073" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:London_westminster_1894.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Layout plan dated 1894</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WestminsterNorth55.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/WestminsterNorth55.jpg/220px-WestminsterNorth55.jpg" width="220" height="340" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/WestminsterNorth55.jpg/330px-WestminsterNorth55.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/WestminsterNorth55.jpg/440px-WestminsterNorth55.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WestminsterNorth55.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>North entrance of Westminster Abbey</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Abbot" title="Abbot">abbot</a> and monks, in proximity to the royal Palace of Westminster, the seat of government from the later 12th century, became a powerful force in the centuries after the Norman Conquest. The <a href="/wiki/Abbot_of_Westminster" title="Abbot of Westminster">Abbot of Westminster</a> often was employed on royal service and in due course took his place in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> as of right. Released from the burdens of spiritual leadership, which passed to the reformed <a href="/wiki/Abbey_of_Cluny" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbey of Cluny">Cluniac movement</a> after the mid-10th century, and occupied with the administration of great landed properties, some of which lay far from Westminster, "the Benedictines achieved a remarkable degree of identification with the secular life of their times, and particularly with upper-class life", Barbara Harvey concludes, to the extent that her depiction of daily life provides a wider view of the concerns of the English gentry in the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High</a> and <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The proximity of the Palace of Westminster did not extend to providing monks or abbots with high royal connections; in social origin the Benedictines of Westminster were as modest as most of the order. The abbot remained <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord of the Manor">Lord of the Manor</a> of Westminster as a town of two to three thousand persons grew around it: as a consumer and employer on a grand scale the monastery helped fuel the town economy, and relations with the town remained unusually cordial, but no enfranchising charter was issued during the Middle Ages.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The abbey became the coronation site of Norman kings. None were buried there until Henry III, intensely devoted to the cult of the Confessor, rebuilt the abbey in <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Anglo-French Gothic style</a> as a shrine to venerate King Edward the Confessor and as a suitably regal setting for Henry\'s own tomb, under the highest Gothic <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> in England. The Confessor\'s shrine subsequently played a great part in his <a href="/wiki/Canonization" title="Canonization">canonization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wpage_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wpage-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The work continued between 1245 and 1517 and was largely finished by the architect <a href="/wiki/Henry_Yevele" title="Henry Yevele">Henry Yevele</a> in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Richard_II_of_England" title="Richard II of England">Richard II</a>. Henry III also commissioned the unique <a href="/wiki/Cosmati" title="Cosmati">Cosmati</a> pavement in front of the High Altar (the pavement has recently undergone a major cleaning and conservation programme and was re-dedicated by the Dean at a service on 21 May 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The building was consecrated on 13 October 1269.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> added a <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Period" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpendicular Period">Perpendicular style</a> chapel dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Mary,_the_mother_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary, the mother of Jesus">Blessed Virgin Mary</a> in 1503 (known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_Chapel" title="Henry VII Chapel">Henry VII Chapel</a></i> or the "Lady Chapel"). Much of the stone came from <a href="/wiki/Caen" title="Caen">Caen</a>, in France (<a href="/wiki/Caen_stone" title="Caen stone">Caen stone</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Portland" title="Isle of Portland">Isle of Portland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portland_stone" title="Portland stone">Portland stone</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Loire_Valley" title="Loire Valley">Loire Valley</a> region of France (<a href="/wiki/Tuffeau_stone" title="Tuffeau stone">tuffeau limestone</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_and_17th_centuries:_dissolution_and_restoration">16th and 17th centuries: dissolution and restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 16th and 17th centuries: dissolution and restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1535, the abbey\'s annual income of \xc2\xa33,000 (equivalent to \xc2\xa31,680,000  as of 2016),<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> during the assessment attendant on the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Monasteries" title="Dissolution of the Monasteries">Dissolution of the Monasteries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1540.E2.80.931550:_10_years_as_a_cathedral"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1540\xe2\x80\x931550:_10_years_as_a_cathedral">1540\xe2\x80\x931550: 10 years as a cathedral</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1540\xe2\x80\x931550: 10 years as a cathedral">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> assumed direct royal control in 1539 and granted the abbey the status of a cathedral by charter in 1540, simultaneously issuing <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">letters patent</a> establishing the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Westminster_(Church_of_England)" title="Diocese of Westminster (Church of England)">Diocese of Westminster</a>. By granting the abbey cathedral status, Henry VIII gained an excuse to spare it from the destruction or dissolution which he inflicted on most English abbeys during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="After_1550:_turbulent_times">After 1550: turbulent times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: After 1550: turbulent times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Westminster diocese was dissolved in 1550, but the abbey was recognised (in 1552, retroactively to 1550) as a second cathedral of the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_London" title="Diocese of London">Diocese of London</a> until 1556.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The already-old expression "<a href="/wiki/To_rob_Peter_to_pay_Paul" title="To rob Peter to pay Paul">robbing Peter to pay Paul</a>" may have been given a new lease of life when money meant for the abbey, which is dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Saint Peter</a>, was diverted to the treasury of <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral" title="St Paul&#39;s Cathedral">St Paul\'s Cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg/250px-Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg/375px-Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg/500px-Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_Interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">Nave</a> of Westminster Abbey</div></div></div>\n<p>The abbey was restored to the Benedictines under the Catholic <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Mary I of England</a>, but they were again ejected under <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I</a> in 1559. In 1560, Elizabeth re-established Westminster as a "<a href="/wiki/Royal_Peculiar" title="Royal Peculiar">Royal Peculiar</a>" \xe2\x80\x93 a church of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> responsible directly to the Sovereign, rather than to a diocesan bishop \xe2\x80\x93 and made it the <b>Collegiate Church of St Peter</b> (that is, a non-cathedral church with an attached chapter of <a href="/wiki/Canon_(priest)" title="Canon (priest)">canons</a>, headed by a dean.)<sup id="cite_ref-peculiar_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peculiar-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It suffered damage during the turbulent 1640s, when it was attacked by <a href="/wiki/Puritan" class="mw-redirect" title="Puritan">Puritan</a> <a href="/wiki/Iconoclasm" title="Iconoclasm">iconoclasts</a>, but was again protected by its close ties to the state during the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth</a> period. <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> was given an elaborate funeral there in 1658, only to be <a href="/wiki/Burial#Exhumation" title="Burial">disinterred</a> in January 1661 and posthumously hanged from a <a href="/wiki/Gibbet" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibbet">gibbet</a> at <a href="/wiki/Tyburn" title="Tyburn">Tyburn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1722.E2.80.931745:_Western_towers_constructed"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1722\xe2\x80\x931745:_Western_towers_constructed">1722\xe2\x80\x931745: Western towers constructed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1722\xe2\x80\x931745: Western towers constructed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The abbey\'s two western towers were built between 1722 and 1745 by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Hawksmoor" title="Nicholas Hawksmoor">Nicholas Hawksmoor</a>, constructed from <a href="/wiki/Portland_stone" title="Portland stone">Portland stone</a> to an early example of a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic Revival">Gothic Revival</a> design. Purbeck marble was used for the walls and the floors of Westminster Abbey, even though the various tombstones are made of different types of marble. Further <a href="/wiki/Victorian_restoration" title="Victorian restoration">rebuilding and restoration</a> occurred in the 19th century under <a href="/wiki/George_Gilbert_Scott" title="George Gilbert Scott">Sir George Gilbert Scott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Narthex" title="Narthex">narthex</a> (a portico or entrance hall) for the west front was designed by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Lutyens" title="Edwin Lutyens">Sir Edwin Lutyens</a> in the mid-20th century but was not built. Images of the abbey prior to the construction of the towers are scarce, though the abbey\'s official website states that the building had "towers which had been left unfinished in the medieval period".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Westminster suffered minor damage during <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">the Blitz</a> on 15 November 1940. Then on May 10/11 1941, the Westminster Abbey precincts and roof were hit by incendiary bombs. All the bombs were extinguished by <a href="/wiki/Air_Raid_Precaution" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Raid Precaution">ARP</a> wardens, except for one bomb which ignited out of reach among the wooden beams and plaster vault of the lantern roof (of 1802) over the North Transept. Flames rapidly spread and burning beams and molten lead began to fall on the wooden stalls, pews and other ecclesiastical fixtures 130 feet below. Despite the falling debris, the staff dragged away as much furniture as possible before withdrawing. Finally the Lantern roof crashed down into the crossing, preventing the fires from spreading further.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war">Post-war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post-war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It was at Westminster Abbey that six companies of eminent churchmen led by <a href="/wiki/Lancelot_Andrewes" title="Lancelot Andrewes">Lancelot Andrewes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dean_of_Westminster" title="Dean of Westminster">Dean of Westminster</a>, had translated the bible into English so creating the <a href="/wiki/King_James_Version" title="King James Version">King James Version</a> in the early 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Joint Committee responsible for assembling the <a href="/wiki/New_English_Bible" title="New English Bible">New English Bible</a> also met twice a year at Westminster Abbey in the 1950s and 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1990s, two icons by the <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russian</a> icon painter <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Fyodorov" title="Sergei Fyodorov">Sergei Fyodorov</a> were hung in the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, the abbey, which was then receiving approximately 1.75 million visitors each year, began charging admission fees to visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 September 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales</a> was held at the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-orderofservice_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orderofservice-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On 17 September 2010, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> became the first pope to set foot in the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2009 the first major building work at the abbey for 250 years was proposed. A <a href="/wiki/Crown_steeple" title="Crown steeple">corona</a> \xe2\x80\x93 a crown-like architectural feature \xe2\x80\x93 was suggested to be built around the <a href="/wiki/Lantern_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lantern (architecture)">lantern</a> over the central <a href="/wiki/Crossing_(architecture)" title="Crossing (architecture)">crossing</a>, replacing an existing pyramidal structure dating from the 1950s. This was part of a wider \xc2\xa323m development of the abbey completed in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>On 4 August 2010 the Dean and Chapter announced that, "[a]fter a considerable amount of preliminary and exploratory work", efforts toward the construction of a corona would not be continued.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, architects Panter Hudspith completed refurbishment of the 14th-century food-store originally used by the abbey\'s monks, converting it into a restaurant with English oak furniture by Covent Garden-based furniture makers <a href="/wiki/Luke_Hughes_(furniture_designer)" title="Luke Hughes (furniture designer)">Luke Hughes and Company</a>. This is now the Cellarium Caf\xc3\xa9 and Terrace.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Queen\'s Diamond Jubilee Galleries have been created in the medieval <a href="/wiki/Triforium" title="Triforium">triforium</a> of the abbey. This is a display area for the abbey\'s treasures in the galleries high up around the abbey\'s nave. A new <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic</a> access tower with lift was designed by the abbey architect and <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_of_the_Fabric_of_Westminster_Abbey" title="Surveyor of the Fabric of Westminster Abbey">Surveyor of the Fabric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_Dean" title="Ptolemy Dean">Ptolemy Dean</a>. The new galleries opened in June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-gallery_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gallery-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul class="gallery /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Westminster Abbey by night, 2009\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronations">Coronations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Coronations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg/220px-SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg/330px-SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg/440px-SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="493" data-file-height="730" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SanktEdvardsstol_westminster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/King_Edward%27s_Chair" class="mw-redirect" title="King Edward&#39;s Chair">King Edward\'s Chair</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_British_monarch" title="Coronation of the British monarch">Coronation of the British monarch</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_coronations" title="List of British coronations">List of British coronations</a></div>\n<p>Since the coronations in 1066 of both <a href="/wiki/Harold_Godwinson" title="Harold Godwinson">King Harold</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a>, every English and British monarch (except <a href="/wiki/Edward_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward V">Edward V</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Edward VIII</a>, who were never crowned) has been crowned in Westminster Abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-History_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coronations_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coronations-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1216, <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a> could not be crowned in London when he came to the throne, because the French prince <a href="/wiki/Louis_VIII_of_France" title="Louis VIII of France">Louis</a> had taken control of the city, and so the king was crowned in <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Cathedral" title="Gloucester Cathedral">Gloucester Cathedral</a>. This coronation was deemed by Pope <a href="/wiki/Honorius_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorius III">Honorius III</a> to be improper, and a further coronation was held in Westminster Abbey on 17 May 1220.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/King_Edward%27s_Chair" class="mw-redirect" title="King Edward&#39;s Chair">King Edward\'s Chair</a> (or St Edward\'s Chair), the throne on which English and British sovereigns have been seated at the moment of crowning, is now housed within the Abbey in St George\'s Chapel near the West Door, and has been used at every coronation since 1308. From 1301 to 1996 (except for a short time in 1950 when the stone was temporarily stolen by <a href="/wiki/Scottish_nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish nationalist">Scottish nationalists</a>), the chair also housed the <a href="/wiki/Stone_of_Scone" title="Stone of Scone">Stone of Scone</a> upon which the kings of Scots are crowned. Although the Stone is now kept in Scotland, in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Castle" title="Edinburgh Castle">Edinburgh Castle</a>, it is intended that the Stone will be returned to St Edward\'s Chair for use during future coronation ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_weddings">Royal weddings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Royal weddings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">Chronology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Chronology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard2_Anna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Richard2_Anna.jpg/220px-Richard2_Anna.jpg" width="220" height="333" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="529" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Richard2_Anna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1382 wedding of <a Prince Andrew, Duke of York, and Sarah Ferguson">23 July 1986</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">Prince Andrew, Duke of York</a>, second son of Queen Elizabeth II</td>\n<td>Miss <a href="/wiki/Sarah,_Duchess_of_York" title="Sarah, Duchess of York">Sarah Ferguson</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Prince_William_and_Catherine_Middleton" title="Wedding of Prince William and Catherine Middleton">29 April 2011</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William, Duke of Cambridge</a>, grandson of Queen Elizabeth II<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>Miss <a href="/wiki/Catherine,_Duchess_of_Cambridge" title="Catherine, Duchess of Cambridge">Catherine Middleton</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dean_and_Chapter">Dean and Chapter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dean and Chapter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dean_and_Chapter_of_Westminster" title="Dean and Chapter of Westminster">Dean and Chapter of Westminster</a></div>\n<p>Westminster Abbey is a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_church" title="Collegiate church">collegiate church</a> governed by the <a href="/wiki/Dean_and_Chapter_of_Westminster" title="Dean and Chapter of Westminster">Dean and Chapter of Westminster</a>, as established by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">Royal charter</a> of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth I">Queen Elizabeth I</a> dated 21 May 1560,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> which created it as the Collegiate Church of St Peter Westminster, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Peculiar" title="Royal Peculiar">Royal Peculiar</a> under the personal jurisdiction of the Sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-peculiar_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peculiar-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The members of the Chapter are the Dean and four canons residentiary;<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> they are assisted by the Receiver General and Chapter Clerk.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> One of the canons is also Rector of <a href="/wiki/St_Margaret%27s,_Westminster" title="St Margaret&#39;s, Westminster">St Margaret\'s Church</a>, Westminster, and often also holds the post of Chaplain to the <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_House_of_Commons_(United_Kingdom)" title="Speaker of the House of Commons (United Kingdom)">Speaker of the House of Commons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the Dean and canons, there are at present three full-time minor canons: the <a href="/wiki/Precentor" title="Precentor">precentor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sacristan" title="Sacristan">sacrist</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chaplain" title="Chaplain">chaplain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-crockford_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crockford-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> A series of Priests Vicar assist the minor canons.<sup id="cite_ref-crockford_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crockford-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Burials_and_memorials">Burials and memorials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Burials and memorials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burials_and_memorials_in_Westminster_Abbey" title="Burials and memorials in Westminster Abbey">Burials and memorials in Westminster Abbey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="413.88117913832" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Dr_John_Hall,_Dean_of_Westminster_on_the_Shrine_of_Edward_the_Confessor.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Dr_John_Hall%2C_Dean_of_Westminster_on_the_Shrine_of_Edward_the_Confessor.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (115 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="114846" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e2/Dr_John_Hall%2C_Dean_of_Westminster_on_the_Shrine_of_Edward_the_Confessor.ogg/Dr_John_Hall%2C_Dean_of_Westminster_on_the_Shrine_of_Edward_the_Confessor.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="172312" /></audio></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_John_Hall,_Dean_of_Westminster_on_the_Shrine_of_Edward_the_Confessor.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Audio description of the shrine of Edward the Confessor by <a href="/wiki/John_Hall_(priest)" title="John Hall (priest)">John Hall</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tombeau_@.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Tombeau_%40.jpg/220px-Tombeau_%40.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Tombeau_%40.jpg/330px-Tombeau_%40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Tombeau_%40.jpg/440px-Tombeau_%40.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tombeau_@.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Recumbent_effigy" class="mw-redirect" title="Recumbent effigy">recumbent effigy</a> on a tomb in Westminster Abbey</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg/220px-Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg/330px-Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg/440px-Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2489" data-file-height="1726" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_cloister.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Cloister" title="Cloister">cloister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">garth</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_England" title="Henry III of England">Henry III</a> rebuilt the abbey in honour of a royal saint, <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a>, whose relics were placed in a <a href="/wiki/Shrine" title="Shrine">shrine</a> in the sanctuary. Henry III himself was interred nearby, as were many of the <a href="/wiki/Plantagenet" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantagenet">Plantagenet</a> kings of England, their wives and other relatives. Until the death of <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">George II</a> in 1760, most kings and queens were buried in the abbey, some notable exceptions being <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward IV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">Henry VIII</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a> who are buried in <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel,_Windsor" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Chapel, Windsor">St George\'s Chapel</a> at <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">Windsor Castle</a>. Other exceptions include <a href="/wiki/Edward_II_of_England" title="Edward II of England">Edward II</a> buried at <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Cathedral" title="Gloucester Cathedral">Gloucester Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John</a> buried at <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Cathedral" title="Worcester Cathedral">Worcester Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_England" title="Henry IV of England">Henry IV</a> buried at <a href="/wiki/Canterbury_Cathedral" title="Canterbury Cathedral">Canterbury Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">Richard III</a>, now buried at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Cathedral" title="Leicester Cathedral">Leicester Cathedral</a>, and the <i>de facto</i> queen <a href="/wiki/Lady_Jane_Grey" title="Lady Jane Grey">Lady Jane Grey</a>, buried in the chapel of <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Peter_ad_Vincula" title="Church of St Peter ad Vincula">St Peter ad Vincula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a>. More recently monarchs have been buried either in St George\'s Chapel or at <a href="/wiki/Frogmore" title="Frogmore">Frogmore</a> to the east of Windsor Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the Middle Ages, aristocrats were buried inside chapels, while monks and other people associated with the abbey were buried in the <a href="/wiki/Cloister" title="Cloister">cloisters</a> and other areas. One of these was <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>, who was buried here as he had apartments in the abbey where he was employed as master of the King\'s Works. Other poets, writers and musicians were buried or memorialised around Chaucer in what became known as <a href="/wiki/Poets%27_Corner" title="Poets&#39; Corner">Poets\' Corner</a>. Abbey musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Henry_Purcell" title="Henry Purcell">Henry Purcell</a> were also buried in their place of work.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Subsequently, it became one of Britain\'s most significant honours to be buried or commemorated in the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-world_and_its_people_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world_and_its_people-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The practice of burying national figures in the abbey began under <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> with the burial of Admiral <a href="/wiki/Robert_Blake_(admiral)" title="Robert Blake (admiral)">Robert Blake</a> in 1657.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The practice spread to include generals, admirals, politicians, doctors and scientists such as <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>, buried on 4 April 1727, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, buried on 26 April 1882, and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a>, buried on 15 June 2018. Another was <a href="/wiki/William_Wilberforce" title="William Wilberforce">William Wilberforce</a> who led the movement to abolish slavery in the United Kingdom and the Plantations, buried on 3 August 1833. Wilberforce was buried in the north transept, close to his friend, the former Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Younger" title="William Pitt the Younger">William Pitt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the early 20th century it became increasingly common to bury <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremated</a> remains rather than coffins in the abbey. In 1905 the actor <a href="/wiki/Henry_Irving" title="Henry Irving">Sir Henry Irving</a> was cremated and his ashes buried in Westminster Abbey, thereby becoming the first person ever to be cremated prior to interment at the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-CremSoc_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CremSoc-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The majority of interments at the Abbey are of cremated remains, but some burials still take place \xe2\x80\x93 Frances Challen, wife of Sebastian Charles, <a href="/wiki/Canon_of_Westminster" class="mw-redirect" title="Canon of Westminster">Canon of Westminster</a>, was buried alongside her husband in the south choir aisle in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-SCharles_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCharles-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Members of the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Northumberland" title="Duke of Northumberland">Percy family</a> have a family vault, <a href="/wiki/The_Northumberland_Vault" class="mw-redirect" title="The Northumberland Vault">The Northumberland Vault</a>, in St Nicholas\'s chapel within the abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the floor, just inside the great west door, in the centre of the nave, is the tomb of <a href="/wiki/The_Unknown_Warrior" title="The Unknown Warrior">The Unknown Warrior</a>, an unidentified British soldier killed on a European battlefield during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>. He was buried in the abbey on 11 November 1920. This grave is the only one in the abbey on which it is forbidden to walk.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the east end of the Lady Chapel is a memorial chapel to the airmen of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> who were killed in the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. It incorporates a memorial window to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>, which replaces an earlier Tudor stained glass window destroyed in the war.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Diana%27s_funeral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diana%27s_funeral.jpg/220px-Diana%27s_funeral.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diana%27s_funeral.jpg/330px-Diana%27s_funeral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Diana%27s_funeral.jpg/440px-Diana%27s_funeral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1795" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Diana%27s_funeral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Funeral procession of Diana, Princess of Wales at Westminster</div></div></div>\n<p>On 6 September 1997 the formal, though not "state" <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales">funeral of Diana, Princess of Wales</a>, was held. It was a royal ceremonial funeral including royal pageantry and Anglican funeral liturgy. A second public service was held on Sunday at the demand of the people. The burial occurred privately later the same day. Diana\'s former husband, sons, mother, siblings, a close friend, and a clergyman were present. Diana\'s body was clothed in a black long-sleeved dress designed by <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Walker_(fashion_designer)" title="Catherine Walker (fashion designer)">Catherine Walker</a>, which she had chosen some weeks before. A set of rosary beads was placed in her hands, a gift she had received from <a href="/wiki/Mother_Teresa" title="Mother Teresa">Mother Teresa</a>, who died a day before Diana\'s funeral. Her grave is on the grounds of her family estate, <a href="/wiki/Althorp" title="Althorp">Althorp</a>, on a private island.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1998 ten vacant statue niches on the fa\xc3\xa7ade above the Great West Door were filled with representative <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey_Burials_and_Memorials#20th_Century_Martyrs" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster Abbey Burials and Memorials">20th-century Christian martyrs</a> of various denominations. Those commemorated are <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Kolbe" title="Maximilian Kolbe">Maximilian Kolbe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manche_Masemola" title="Manche Masemola">Manche Masemola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janani_Luwum" title="Janani Luwum">Janani Luwum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchess_Elizabeth_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duchess Elizabeth of Russia">Grand Duchess Elizabeth of Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr." title="Martin Luther King Jr.">Martin Luther King Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="\xc3\x93scar Romero">\xc3\x93scar Romero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Bonhoeffer" title="Dietrich Bonhoeffer">Dietrich Bonhoeffer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esther_John" title="Esther John">Esther John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucian_Tapiedi" title="Lucian Tapiedi">Lucian Tapiedi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wang_Zhiming_(Christian)" title="Wang Zhiming (Christian)">Wang Zhiming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 9 April 2002 the <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Funeral of Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">ceremonial funeral of Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother</a> was held in the abbey. She was interred later the same day in the <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel,_Windsor_Castle#King_George_VI_Memorial_Chapel" title="St George&#39;s Chapel, Windsor Castle">King George VI Memorial Chapel</a> at <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Chapel,_Windsor_Castle" title="St George&#39;s Chapel, Windsor Castle">St George\'s Chapel, Windsor Castle</a> next to her husband, <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a>, who had died 50 years previously. At the same time, the ashes of the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">Queen Mother</a>\'s daughter, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret,_Countess_of_Snowdon" title="Princess Margaret, Countess of Snowdon">Princess Margaret, Countess of Snowdon</a>, who had died on 9 February 2002, were also interred in a private family service.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Westminster_School" title="Westminster School">Westminster School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey_Choir_School" title="Westminster Abbey Choir School">Westminster Abbey Choir School</a> are also in the precincts of the abbey. The Choir School educates and trains the choirboys who sing for services in the Abbey.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Westminster Abbey is renowned for its choral tradition, and the repertoire of <a href="/wiki/Anglican_church_music" title="Anglican church music">Anglican church music</a> is heard in daily worship, particularly at the service of <a href="/wiki/Choral_Evensong" class="mw-redirect" title="Choral Evensong">Choral Evensong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organ">Organ</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Organ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Westminster_Abbey_organists" title="List of Westminster Abbey organists">List of Westminster Abbey organists</a></div>\n<p>The organ was built by <a href="/wiki/Harrison_%26_Harrison" title="Harrison &amp; Harrison">Harrison &amp; Harrison</a> in 1937, then with four manuals and 84 speaking stops, and was used for the first time at the coronation of <a href="/wiki/King_George_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="King George VI">King George VI</a>. Some pipework from the previous Hill organ of 1848 was revoiced and incorporated in the new scheme. The two organ cases, designed and built in the late 19th century by <a href="/wiki/John_Loughborough_Pearson" title="John Loughborough Pearson">John Loughborough Pearson</a>, were re-instated and coloured in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1982 and 1987, Harrison and Harrison enlarged the organ under the direction of the then abbey organist <a href="/wiki/Simon_Preston" title="Simon Preston">Simon Preston</a> to include an additional Lower Choir Organ and a Bombarde Organ: the current instrument now has five manuals and 109 speaking stops. In 2006, the console of the organ was refurbished by Harrison and Harrison, and space was prepared for two additional 16&#160;ft stops on the Lower Choir Organ and the Bombarde Organ.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current <a href="/wiki/Organist_and_Master_of_the_Choristers" title="Organist and Master of the Choristers">Organist and Master of the Choristers</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_O%27Donnell_(organist)" title="James O&#39;Donnell (organist)">James O\'Donnell</a>, has been in post since 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bells">Bells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Bells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The bells at the abbey were overhauled in 1971. The <a href="/wiki/Ring_of_bells" title="Ring of bells">ring</a> is now made up of ten bells, hung for <a href="/wiki/Change_ringing" title="Change ringing">change ringing</a>, cast in 1971, by the <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_Bell_Foundry" title="Whitechapel Bell Foundry">Whitechapel Bell Foundry</a>, tuned to the notes: F#, E, D, C#, B, A, G, F#, E and D. The Tenor bell in D (588.5&#160;Hz) has a weight of 30&#160;cwt, 1&#160;qtr, 15&#160;lb (3403&#160;lb or 1544&#160;kg).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition there are two service bells, cast by Robert Mot, in 1585 and 1598 respectively, a Sanctus bell cast in 1738 by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Phelps_(bell-founder)" title="Richard Phelps (bell-founder)">Richard Phelps</a> and Thomas Lester and two unused bells\xe2\x80\x94one cast about 1320, by the successor to R de Wymbish, and a second cast in 1742, by Thomas Lester.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The two service bells and the 1320 bell, along with a fourth small silver "dish bell", kept in the refectory, have been noted as being of historical importance by the Church Buildings Council of the Church of England.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chapter_house">Chapter house</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chapter house">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG/220px-Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG/330px-Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG/440px-Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_Chapter_House_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chapter house</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chapter_house" title="Chapter house">chapter house</a> was built concurrently with the east parts of the abbey under Henry III, between about 1245 and 1253.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1863_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1863-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It was <a href="/wiki/Victorian_restoration" title="Victorian restoration">restored</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Gilbert_Scott" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir George Gilbert Scott">Sir George Gilbert Scott</a> in 1872. The entrance is approached from the east cloister walk and includes a double doorway with a large tympanum above.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1863_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1863-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Inner and outer vestibules lead to the octagonal chapter house, which is of exceptional architectural purity. It is built in a Geometrical Gothic style with an octagonal crypt below. A pier of eight shafts carries the vaulted ceiling. To the sides are blind arcading, remains of 14th-century paintings and numerous stone benches above which are innovatory large 4-light quatre-foiled windows.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1863_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1863-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> These are virtually contemporary with the <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Chapelle" title="Sainte-Chapelle">Sainte-Chapelle</a>, Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1863_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1863-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The chapter house has an original mid-13th-century tiled pavement. A door within the vestibule dates from around 1050 and is believed to be the oldest in England.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The exterior includes flying buttresses added in the 14th century and a leaded tent-lantern roof on an iron frame designed by Scott. The Chapter house was originally used in the 13th century by Benedictine monks for daily meetings. It later became a meeting place of the King\'s Great Council and the Commons, predecessors of Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-eh_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eh-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Pyx Chamber formed the undercroft of the monks\' dormitory. It dates to the late 11th century and was used as a monastic and royal treasury. The outer walls and circular piers are of 11th-century date, several of the capitals were enriched in the 12th century and the stone altar added in the 13th century. The term <i>pyx</i> refers to the boxwood chest in which coins were held and presented to a jury during the <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_the_Pyx" title="Trial of the Pyx">Trial of the Pyx</a>, in which newly minted coins were presented to ensure they conformed to the required standards.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The chapter house and Pyx Chamber at Westminster Abbey are in the guardianship of <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a>, but under the care and management of the Dean and Chapter of Westminster.<sup id="cite_ref-eh_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eh-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museum">Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Westminster_Abbey&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey_Museum" title="Westminster Abbey Museum">Westminster Abbey Museum</a> was located in the 11th-century <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vaulted</a> <a href="/wiki/Undercroft" title="Undercroft">undercroft</a> beneath the former monks\' dormitory in Westminster Abbey. This was one of the oldest areas of the abbey, dating back almost to the foundation of the church by <a href="/wiki/Edward_the_Confessor" title="Edward the Confessor">Edward the Confessor</a> in 1065. This space had been used as a museum since 1908<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> but was closed to the public in June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-gallery_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gallery-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span style="width: 115.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 113.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westminster_Abbey_-_Aug_2013.jpg" class="image"><img
